< Text>
Between the relatively 'sceneic' exercise trail around the exterior of park; spacious fields for soccer or baseball activities; solo tennis court.....and executive 3-part playground for the wee lil lads- I'd say this park has a great blend of everything for every type of person wanting to enjoy the urban outdoors.
The bathrooms are done by [www . publicrestroomcompany . com] ...so you know that the facilities are gonna be reliably in order. Lol

HOWEVER~
This park gets only a 4/5 star rating from me because of the dyslexic design of the basketball 'court' .... The court is shaped like a boomerang and requires you to shoot free throws 2.5 feet's to the left in order to be straight-on with the hoop. Any real hooper dribbling around on this court would feel awkward. Oh, and one of the rims is so loosey goosey (rattles every non-swish shot)...you better hope u score the 1 good hoop or you've just flushed your practice sesh. Attached are pics of the botched bball court ..

PS contrary to popular belief, the morning physical trainer guy isn't that bad. Just tell him that he's in the way. He'll move.<//Text>

< Text>
Although the sign says "eclectic", and indeed some dishes are slightly less conventional, this is much more good, solid mom & pop cuisine for slightly more daring families.
If you expect avant-garde fusion, this is not your place.
Nouvelle cuisine this ain't, but rather a very good, place for interesting food with a Mexican heritage.
Everything we had tasted very good, was well executed and tasted freshly made.
Even the chips and salsa, with the salsa nice and hot, not just out of a can.
Definitely a place we'll visit again.
Before you get upset because they're not serving you, please note the Order Here sign, you order at the counter, not the table.</Text>

<Name>Viet Nguyen<//Name><rating>4<//rating>< response>
None</response>
< text>
Opted for the ceviche tostada ($11.95) and tamales ($13.95).
Ceviche was very refreshing, with the fresh white fish and shrimp tasting spectacular among the diced onions, cilantro, and tomatoes. Tostadas were toasted well. My only gripe about this dish is that they put too much lime in it, to the point where it was all I could taste. If there was an option to have lime on the side so I could add as much as I wanted, that would be nice.
Tamales were on point! Pork mole was excellent, and the chicken chile verde was moist and not too stringy. But the winner of this dish had to be the rice and the slight kick it brought with each bite.< /text>

< text>
This place is really cool for Magic the Gathering. It reminds me of my time visiting Star City Games in Roanoke, VA. They are that good. They give fair pricing on pre-orders, they sell singles based on TCG player prices, they do Friday Night Magic with extra prizes (in Discord during this Pandemic time), their Magic community knows what they are talking about, and their staff answers all questions through phone, Discord, or in person. They also have a lot of nice board games and I bought a couple from here. I missed Magic the Gathering when I came to Ventura County and visited a couple of shops around here, but I would say that these guys do it the best in this county. I believe this so much so that I have been willing to make the extra long trip from west Ventura to visit this store.<//text>

< user_name>
Veronica G<//user_name>
<time>1467615702180<//time><Rating>5</Rating>< review>
Let me start off by saying that I have seen and reviewed THOUSANDS and THOUSANDS of international wedding photos thanks to my previous job at a photobook company. If you have good looking people in nice clothes, a beautiful backdrop, and high quality camera with autofocus, it is not that difficult to take pretty photos. After being exposed to the same pretty yet ordinary wedding photos for years, I knew I wanted photographers with a different approach and style- photographers who knew how to steal moments of explosive emotions or thoughts besides "I hope I don't look fat."

There are SO MANY photographers in the bay area. I started by looking at portfolios and moving on to blogs, social media, and anything I could find on them (It is so important to look beyond their portfolios- that only displays their select very best work!!). After narrowing my options down, I finally stumbled upon Choco Studios on yelp. While their portfolio is amazing, it was their blog and photos I found on google that reeled me in. They met all my criteria- 1) Unique approach & style 2) Experience with taking equally beautiful photos in natural light + artificial light 3) Experience in capturing diverse/multiethnic weddings (We had a Mexican/Indian wedding) 4) Affordable price. I quickly made an appointment and booked Mike and Nat on the spot.

Mike and Nat go far beyond taking "pretty photos". Indeed, what they can capture in raw photos is exceptional, but it is also their skills in photo editing software that contribute to their unique style. I truly believe that photography is what they were meant for; they have an intuitive nature of knowing the exact moment of when to take photos- when you are looking at the photos later, it truly is like reliving your special day. And their abilities go beyond capturing the bride & groom wonderfully- we have the most amazing photos of guests as well!

Lastly, on our wedding day, we had a few things go wrong with other vendors, but we were able to count on Mike and Nat to be professional and do an amazing job smoothly, despite messy situations. I cannot recommend Mike and Nat enough!<//review>

Karina was such a great host, very attentive and nice.  Since this was my first time, went for the Lomo Saltado.  It didn't take long for the hot plate to come. They have 2 sauces tableside: a jalape√±o-based aioli and a huacatay sauce.  Both were incredibly flavorful, with the huacatay being spicier.  I wanted to take the bottles with me, but that would have been rude (but I would have been totally justified).
I'll definitely come back with the family and order everything else.  A must stop if you are in the area.</Review>

<text>The Baked Potato is a jazz institution in LA!
As one of the city‚Äôs most frost formidable and long standing jazz bars, it host a variety of modern and veteran jazz and jazz/rock/fusion players from around the globe. The decor is full of authentic memorabilia dating back many decades with original signatures on most of the photographs. The sound is incredible and is well balanced through the entire club with attention to detail. There is no bad seat anywhere, great views from front left and right of the band. This is one of LA's best secrets! If you like jazz, blues, or best of all fusion, there's no place like the baked potato! Baking at the Potato, as they say. An intimate venue, don't come if your claustrophobic. It's about the size of Grandma's living room. Everybody that plays here is a veritable legend. And they serve up a hundred varieties of baked potatoes. With a full bar and two drink minimum, it's downright cozy. This is the place for serious music fans.</Text>

<Rating>3<//Rating><Review>Saw a great show here but this place is too small, too crowded and too expensive. Im sure they are trying to get as many people in that they can, but removing 1 bar stool and about 4 or 5 chairs would do wonders for their customers comfort and enjoyment.

Instead of being able to really direct my full attention to the musicians working hard in front of me, I had to prop myself into half a spot at the bar where the required meal was served and there was no room to eat it, which turned out to not be the worst thing (more on that below), I couldn't sit on the bar stool or I'd have blocked the aisle, the host tripped over my foot that had nowhere to go (sorry brother. )  Both of my legs fell asleep along with my backside, tried to stand but that blocked the way. Needed to stay by my food so moving was out and it's not like there was anywhere to go.

About the food, when they named this place the baked potato they must have signed a non-compete with any other foods as every entr√©e is served on a baked potato. I love baked potatoes, except this one, it's just not a good base for everything. I had the "special" chicken fajitas potato which was a dry unfortunate creation and I can't imagine chicken fajitas with butter which was suggested as a moistener. It's almost like they are afraid to put anything else on the menu for fear of learning what a bad idea the all potato theme is. Lack of food and physical discomfort due to poor thinking and greed resulted in an evening that I have no desire to repeat. It's a shame, I'm a native angeleno and I've heard about the baked potato since I was a youngster, the best I can say is checked that off the list. The barman was very attentive, the waitresses seemed to be on top of things, the host left us standing by the door to be seated and my saintly girlfriend ended up going to find him. <Review>One of the best live music venues in all of California. It's quite small about 70ish seats, but because of it the musicians are right there jamming in front of you only a few feet away, it truly allows for such a unique experience and provides some of the best sounding live music I've had the chance to enjoy.

There is a 2 drink minimum per person, but 1 of the drinks can be substituted for dessert if they have any available, due to limited supply. If you're hungry they have these gargantuan potatoes each with an assortment of toppings as well as some different salads. The prices are very reasonable and the portions are very generous. The drinks are also very strong without being over priced which is always good, they also have a pretty decent selection of wines and beer along with the usual spirits for cocktails or whatever.

I can't reccomend this place enough, if you have the opportunity to see a show here don't pass it up you'll regret it believe me.<//Review></record></dataset><record>

<user>112258607976224407186</user><user_name>Noah Rifkin</user_name>< Date>
1403960801646<//Date>
<Rating>5< /Rating>< review>
I have been frequenting this place since I was old enough to drive: seeing the likes of Dave & Done Grusin, Lee Rittenour, Patrice Rushen, Abe Laboriel, & Larry Carloton.  it is one of THE best places to see this kind of music in the entire region.

There used to be so many of these clubs but now, so few.  But the Baked Potato was ALWAYS, a step apart.

The quality of the music is their goal not the glitz and comfort!   Justin's effort's, taking over from his dad, are consistent!.  This is the place to go see --  not hot top 10 folks -- but the truly skilled: the musician's musicians.

These are the people who hollywood studios turn to when they need to drop a piece of music in front of them with a movie screen playing before them and say, "Take it from the top -- we're doing this in one take."

An understated homey and warm place to be with friends.  One of the
BEST!  No pretense whatsoever!  You see what you get and you get what you see!<//review>
